The host environment (Claude, Codex, Gemini, Cursor) remains the execution container. Wazir supplies the operating model, guardrails, and artifact contracts.\n     4→\n     5→## Core components\n     6→\n     7→| Component | Purpose |\n     8→|-----------|---------|\n     9→| Roles | Canonical contracts defining what each agent role does and produces |\n    10→| Workflows | Phase entrypoints that sequence roles through delivery |\n    11→| Skills | Reusable procedures (wz:tdd, wz:debugging, wz:verification, wz:brainstorming) |\n    12→| Hooks | Guardrails enforcing protected paths, loop caps, and capture routing |\n    13→| Expertise | 315 curated knowledge modules composed into agent prompts |\n    14→| Templates | Artifact templates for phase outputs and handoff |\n    15→| Schemas | Validation schemas for manifest, hooks, artifacts, and exports |\n    16→| Exports | Generated host packages tailored per supported host |\n    17→| Tooling | CLI for validation, indexing, recall, capture, and status |\n    18→\n    19→## Design influences\n    20→\n    21→| Source | What Wazir keeps |\n    22→|--------|----------------------|\n    23→| Wazir skill system | Disciplined workflows, TDD, verification, review rigor, skill ergonomics |\n    24→| Spec-Kit | Spec-first development, explicit artifacts, approval gates |\n    25→| Oh My Claude | Host-native prompt structure and operator ergonomics |\n    26→| autoresearch | Research loops, experiment tracking, self-improvement discipline |\n    27→\n    28→## Context and indexing\n    29→\n    30→Wazir ships a built-in local index and recall surface that reduces context window consumption by 60-80% on exploration-heavy phases.\n    31→\n    32→### Context tiers\n    33→\n    34→| Tier | Token budget | Content | When to use |\n    35→|------|-------------|---------|-------------|\n    36→| L0 | ~100 tokens | One-line identifier (name, kind, language, line range) | Inventory scans, deciding what to load |\n    37→| L1 | ~500-2k tokens | Structural summary (signature, fields, purpose, dependencies) | Understanding shape without full source |\n    38→| L2 | Full content | Exact line-bounded source slice | Implementation, debugging, code review |\n    39→\n    40→### Role-specific recall defaults\n    41→\n    42→Roles are assigned default tiers based on their information needs:\n    43→\n    44→- **Exploration roles** (clarifier, researcher, specifier, content-author, designer, planner) default to L1 -- they need to understand structure across many files without reading every line\n    45→- **Implementation roles** (executor, verifier) default to direct read (L2) -- they need exact source for code changes and verification\n    46→- **Review role** (reviewer) starts at L1 as a triage pass, escalating to direct read only for logic errors, security concerns, or ambiguous summaries\n    47→- **Learning role** (learner) defaults to L0 -- it needs only inventory-level context to identify what changed\n    48→\n    49→Every role includes a fallback chain: if the preferred tier fails (no index, no summaries), the role falls back to direct file reads. The system degrades gracefully -- no wasted tokens on failed index operations.\n    50→\n    51→### Capture routing\n    52→\n    53→Large tool output is routed to run-local files via `wazir capture route` and `wazir capture output`, keeping the context window lean. The agent receives a file path reference (~50 tokens) instead of the full output.\n    54→\n    55→### Pipeline integration points\n    56→\n    57→The index and recall surface integrates with the pipeline at five points:\n    58→\n    59→1. **Session start** -- the bootstrap hook runs `index refresh` (or `build` for first run) to ensure the index is current\n    60→2. **Scan project** -- the `scan-project` skill runs `index stats` to report index health in the project profile\n    61→3. **Debugging** -- the `wz:debugging` OBSERVE phase uses `index search-symbols` and `recall --tier L1` for symbol-first exploration\n    62→4. **Execute** -- the executor uses `recall file` and `recall symbol` for targeted source reads\n    63→5. **Verify** -- the verifier uses direct reads for full validation\n    64→\n    65→### Measuring savings\n    66→\n    67→`wazir capture usage` generates a per-run token savings report showing capture routing statistics and context window savings. This provides concrete evidence of token reduction per session.\n    68→\n    69→The context-mode integration remains an optional adapter -- off by default, never required for core install, build, or test paths.\n    70→\n    71→See [Indexing and Recall](indexing-and-recall.md) for full command details and extractor documentation.\n    72→\n    73→## Design Phase\n    74→\n    75→The design phase runs after specification and before planning. The `designer` role uses open-pencil MCP tools to produce visual designs from the approved spec. Outputs include a `.fig` design file, exported Tailwind JSX/HTML+CSS scaffolds, design tokens JSON, and screenshot PNGs.\n    76→\n    77→The `design-review` workflow validates designs against the spec before planning begins. The existing `review` workflow also checks design-vs-implementation alignment after execution.\n    78→\n    79→open-pencil is integrated as an optional adapter (`open_pencil`) — it is not required for core Wazir functionality.\n    80→\n    81→## Key references\n    82→\n    83→- [Roles & Workflows](roles-and-workflows.md)\n    84→- [Artifact Model](artifact-model.md)\n    85→- [Host Exports](../reference/host-exports.md)\n    86→- [Hooks](../reference/hooks.md)\n    87→- [Expertise & Antipatterns](composition-engine.md)\n    88→"}]},"uuid":"cacff975-1754-4189-aa70-89065dbb4944","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:33:20.823Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"0d2b11c1-0980-46b7-982b-f1a99e731ff2","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}

{"parentUuid":"3999815b-71e3-415f-9ab9-c9eb360de5f9","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"a18fb002157904af5","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_01WpdF2gVgTBNurLXXNeNqAs","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"\n\nI now have complete understanding of the existing system. Let me compile the full research output.\n\n---\n\n## Research Report: State Machines for Agent Pipeline Enforcement\n\n### Part 1: Current Wazir State Architecture (Baseline)\n\n**What exists today:**\n\nThe system already has substantial state infrastructure spread across multiple files:\n\n| Component | Location | Role |\n|-----------|----------|------|\n| `status.json` | `~/.wazir/projects/{slug}/runs/{run-id}/status.json` | Current run state (phase, status, loop counts, artifacts) |\n| `events.ndjson` | Same run directory | Append-only event log (phase_enter, phase_exit, gate_approved, gate_rejected, loop_iteration) |\n| `decisions.ndjson` | Same run directory | Append-only decision log |\n| `state.sqlite` | `~/.wazir/projects/{slug}/state/state.sqlite` | Cross-run persistent state (learnings, findings, audit history, usage) |\n| `run-config.yaml` | Same run directory | Per-run policy overrides (loop caps, enabled workflows) |\n| `latest` | `~/.wazir/projects/{slug}/runs/latest` | Text file with most recent run ID for session recovery |\n\n**What exists for enforcement:**\n- `phase-prerequisite-guard.js` -- checks required artifacts exist and proofs pass before allowing `phase_enter` events (exit code 44 on failure)\n- `loop-cap-guard.js` -- prevents phase loops from exceeding configured caps (exit code 43)\n- `gating/agent.js` -- evaluates phase reports against `gating-rules.yaml` to produce `continue`/`loop_back`/`escalate` verdicts\n- `validateRunCompletion()` -- checks all enabled workflows have phase_exit events before summary finalization\n\n**The gap:** There is no single `pipeline-state.json` that represents the full state machine. The current `status.json` tracks the *current* position but does not encode:\n1. Which gates have been passed (and by whom)\n2. The full phase transition graph with timestamps\n3. Session isolation (no session_id)\n4. Rejection/retry history\n5. Atomic write safety\n\nHooks currently read `status.json` + scan `events.ndjson` independently. This works but is O(n) on events and lacks a single-read \"is this phase allowed?\" answer.\n\n---\n\n### Part 2: Temporal.io Event Sourcing Model (Research)\n\n**How Temporal tracks workflow state:**\n\nTemporal uses a deterministic replay model built on an append-only event history. Key design properties:\n\n1. **Event History is the single source of truth.** There is no separate \"state\" object. Workflow state is reconstructed by replaying the event history from the beginning. Each event has:\n   - `event_id` (monotonically increasing integer)\n   - `event_type` (e.g., `WorkflowExecutionStarted`, `ActivityTaskScheduled`, `ActivityTaskCompleted`, `TimerFired`)\n   - `timestamp` (wall-clock time of recording)\n   - `attributes` (type-specific payload)\n\n2. **Deterministic replay for recovery.** When a worker crashes and restarts, Temporal replays the full event history through the workflow function. The function must be deterministic -- given the same events, it produces the same state. Side effects (activities, timers, signals) are recorded as events, so replay skips re-executing them.\n\n3. **Concurrent access is solved by \"workflow task\" exclusivity.** Only one \"workflow task\" (decision task) runs at a time per workflow execution. The Temporal server serializes all mutations through this single-threaded model. No two workers can simultaneously modify the same workflow's state.\n\n4. **Activity ordering enforced by explicit `await`.** Each activity call suspends the workflow function until the activity completes (recorded as an `ActivityTaskCompleted` event). Sequential activities are just sequential awaits. Parallel activities use `Promise.all()`.\n\n5. **Saga pattern for compensation.** When a step fails, Temporal supports compensating transactions (sagas) -- each completed step records enough info to undo it.\n\n**What Wazir can adopt (simplified):**\n\n- **Don't replay events to reconstruct state.** Temporal's replay is for distributed systems where workers are stateless. Wazir runs locally -- we can maintain a materialized state document.\n- **Do adopt the append-only event log as audit trail** (already done via `events.ndjson`).\n- **Do adopt the \"single source of truth\" principle** -- one file (`pipeline-state.json`) that is the materialized view of the event log. Hooks read ONLY this file, never scan events.ndjson.\n- **Do adopt monotonic event IDs** -- each event gets a sequence number, and `pipeline-state.json` records the `last_event_seq` it was materialized from. This enables consistency checks.\n\n---\n\n### Part 3: GitHub Actions Job State Model (Research)\n\n**How GitHub Actions tracks job state:**\n\n1. **`needs` keyword declares DAG edges.** A job with `needs: [build, test]` will not start until both `build` and `test` complete successfully. This is a static DAG defined in YAML, resolved at workflow dispatch time.\n\n2. **Job states:** `queued` -> `in_progress` -> `completed` (with conclusion: `success`, `failure`, `cancelled`, `skipped`). Each job also has `steps` with the same state model.\n\n3. **State is centralized in the workflow run object.** The GitHub Actions runtime maintains a single workflow run record with all job statuses. When a job completes, the orchestrator checks which downstream jobs now have all `needs` satisfied and queues them.\n\n4. **Concurrency control** uses a `concurrency` key with a group string. Only one run per concurrency group can be `in_progress` at a time. Others queue or cancel.\n\n5. **Conditional execution** via `if:` expressions that can read `needs.<job>.result` to branch on upstream outcomes.\n\n**What Wazir can adopt:**\n\n- **Static DAG + runtime state = separation of concerns.** The pipeline definition (which phase follows which, which gates exist) is already in `pipeline.mdc` and the manifest. The runtime state should be a separate document that tracks positions in that DAG.\n- **Explicit `needs`-style prerequisite declaration.** Already partially done in `phase_prerequisites` in the manifest, but only for the 4 macro-phases. Should extend to all 14 workflow steps.\n- **Job conclusion model.** Each phase should have a `conclusion` field: `success`, `failure`, `skipped`, `rejected` (gate-specific). This is richer than the current `completed` status.\n- **Concurrency group = session_id.** GitHub Actions' concurrency groups map perfectly to session isolation.\n\n---\n\n### Part 4: Concrete Schema for `pipeline-state.json`\n\nBased on the above research, here is the proposed schema. Design principles:\n- **Single file, single read.** Hooks read this file to answer \"can I enter phase X?\" in O(1).\n- **CLI writes, hooks only read.** Only `wazir capture` commands mutate this file.\n- **Atomic writes via temp+rename.** Write to `.pipeline-state.json.tmp`, then `rename()`.\n- **Session-isolated.** Each session must match `session_id` or the file is treated as stale.\n- **Crash-recoverable.** The file is always valid JSON (atomic writes guarantee this). The `events.ndjson` log is the recovery source if the file is ever corrupted.\n\n```json\n{\n  \"$schema\": \"https://wazir.dev/schemas/pipeline-state.schema.json\",\n  \"schema_version\": 1,\n\n  \"run_id\": \"run-20260320-143000\",\n  \"session_id\": \"ses-a1b2c3d4\",\n  \"project_root\": \"/Users/dev/myproject\",\n\n  \"current_phase\": \"plan\",\n  \"current_phase_status\": \"in_progress\",\n  \"current_role\": \"planner\",\n\n  \"phase_sequence\": [\n    \"clarify\", \"discover\", \"specify\", \"spec-challenge\",\n    \"author\", \"design\", \"design-review\",\n    \"plan\", \"plan-review\",\n    \"execute\", \"verify\", \"review\", \"learn\", \"prepare-next\"\n  ],\n\n  \"phases\": {\n    \"clarify\": {\n      \"status\": \"completed\",\n      \"conclusion\": \"success\",\n      \"entered_at\": \"2026-03-20T14:30:00.000Z\",\n      \"exited_at\": \"2026-03-20T14:32:00.000Z\",\n      \"role\": \"clarifier\",\n      \"loop_count\": 2,\n and Rationale\n\n#### Top-level fields\n\n| Field | Type | Purpose | Rationale |\n|-------|------|---------|-----------|\n| `schema_version` | integer | Forward compatibility | Allows hooks to reject files from incompatible versions |\n| `run_id` | string | Run identifier | Already exists in status.json; carried forward |\n| `session_id` | string | Session isolation key | Prevents stale reads from a different session/agent |\n| `project_root` | string | Absolute path to project | Already exists; needed for artifact path resolution |\n| `current_phase` | string | Active phase name | The single-read answer to \"where are we now?\" |\n| `current_phase_status` | enum | `in_progress`, `waiting_gate`, `completed`, `failed` | Richer than current `status` field |\n| `current_role` | string | Active role | Hooks can enforce role-specific constraints |\n| `phase_sequence` | string[] | Ordered list of all phases | Embedded DAG definition; hooks don't need to read pipeline.mdc |\n\n#### Per-phase object\n\n| Field | Type | Purpose |\n|-------|------|---------|\n| `status` | enum: `pending`, `blocked`, `in_progress`, `waiting_gate`, `completed`, `skipped`, `failed` | Phase lifecycle state |\n| `conclusion` | enum: `success`, `failure`, `approved`, `rejected`, `skipped`, null | Terminal outcome (inspired by GitHub Actions) |\n| `entered_at` / `exited_at` | ISO 8601 timestamp | Duration tracking, freshness checks |\n| `role` | string | Which role executed this phase |\n| `loop_count` | integer | Current loop iteration (replaces scattered `phase_loop_counts`) |\n| `artifacts_produced` | string[] | Paths relative to run root; enables prerequisite checking without scanning disk |\n| `gate` | object or null | Gate decision record for approval-gate phases |\n\n#### Gate object (for spec-challenge, design-review, plan-review)\n\n| Field | Type | Purpose |\n|-------|------|---------|\n| `type` | enum: `approval` | Gate type (extensible for future gate types) |\n| `verdict` | enum: `approved`, `rejected`, `pending` | Current verdict |\n| `decided_at` | ISO 8601 timestamp | When the verdict was rendered |\n| `decided_by` | string | Model/agent that made the decision (enforces \"reviewer is never the author\") |\n| `rejection_count` | integer | How many times this gate was rejected before approval |\n| `rejection_history` | array of `{at, reason, by}` | Full rejection trail for audit |\n\n#### Derived convenience fields\n\n| Field | Type | Purpose |\n|-------|------|---------|\n| `gates_passed` | string[] | Quick check: has spec-challenge been approved? |\n| `gates_pending` | string[] | Which gates still block progress? |\n| `last_event_seq` | integer | Monotonic event counter; enables consistency check against events.ndjson |\n| `last_event_type` | string | Most recent event type for quick status display |\n| `integrity.event_count` | integer | Total events materialized into this state |\n| `integrity.checksum` | string | SHA-256 of events.ndjson up to `last_event_seq`; enables corruption detection |\n\n---\n\n### Part 6: Update Rules (Who Writes, When)\n\n**Principle: CLI commands are the only writers. Hooks never write.**\n\n| Trigger | CLI Command | State Mutation |\n|---------|------------|----------------|\n| Run init | `wazir capture init` | Create file with all phases in `pending`, set `current_phase` |\n| Phase enter | `wazir capture event --event phase_enter` | Set phase to `in_progress`, update `current_phase`, record `entered_at` |\n| Phase exit | `wazir capture event --event phase_exit` | Set phase to `completed`/`failed`, record `exited_at`, advance `current_phase` to next |\n| Gate approved | `wazir capture event --event gate_approved` | Set phase conclusion to `approved`, add to `gates_passed`, remove from `gates_pending`, set gate object |\n| Gate rejected | `wazir capture event --event gate_rejected` | Set phase conclusion to `rejected`, increment `rejection_count`, append to `rejection_history`, set current phase back to the rework target |\n| Loop iteration | `wazir capture loop-check` | Increment `loop_count` for current phase |\n| Session start | `wazir capture init` or resume | Set/validate `session_id` |\n\n**Atomic write protocol:**\n\n```\n1. Read current pipeline-state.json\n2. Apply mutation in memory\n3. Increment last_event_seq\n4. Write to pipeline-state.json.tmp (same directory, same filesystem)\n5. fsync the temp file\n6. rename() temp -> pipeline-state.json  (atomic on POSIX)\n```\n\nThis guarantees that hooks always read a complete, valid JSON file. If the CLI crashes between steps 4 and 6, the old file remains intact. On next startup, the CLI detects `last_event_seq` < `events.ndjson` line count and replays missing events to rebuild state.\n\n---\n\n### Part 7: Read Patterns for Hooks\n\n**Hook read protocol:**\n\n```javascript\nfunction readPipelineState(stateRoot, runId) {\n  const statePath = path.join(stateRoot, 'runs', runId, 'pipeline-state.json');\n  if (!fs.existsSync(statePath)) return null; // standalone mode\n  return JSON.parse(fs.readFileSync(statePath, 'utf8'));\n}\n```\n\n**Phase prerequisite check (replaces current events.ndjson scan):**\n\n```javascript\nfunction canEnterPhase(state, targetPhase) {\n  // 1. Check phase_sequence ordering\n  const targetIndex = state.phase_sequence.indexOf(targetPhase);\n  const currentIndex = state.phase_sequence.indexOf(state.current_phase);\n  \n  // Can't skip ahead (unless all intermediate phases are completed/skipped)\n  for (let i = 0; i < targetIndex; i++) {\n    const phase = state.phase_sequence[i];\n    const phaseState = state.phases[phase];\n    if (!phaseState) continue;\n    if (!['completed', 'skipped'].includes(phaseState.status)) {\n      return { allowed: false, reason: `Phase ${phase} not completed (status: ${phaseState.status})` };\n    }\n  }\n\n  // 2. Check gates\n  const gatePhases = ['spec-challenge', 'design-review', 'plan-review'];\n  for (const gate of gatePhases) {\n    const gateIndex = state.phase_sequence.indexOf(gate);\n    if (gateIndex < targetIndex && !state.gates_passed.includes(gate)) {\n      return { allowed: false, reason: `Gate ${gate} not yet passed` };\n    }\n  }\n\n  return { allowed: true };\n}\n```\n\n**Session isolation check:**\n\n```javascript\nfunction validateSession(state, currentSessionId) {\n  if (state.session_id !== currentSessionId) {\n    return {\n      valid: false,\n      reason: `Session mismatch: state has ${state.session_id}, current is ${currentSessionId}`,\n      recovery: 'stale_session'\n    };\n  }\n  return { valid: true };\n}\n```\n\n**Loop cap check (replaces current status.json scan):**\n\n```javascript\nfunction checkLoopCap(state, phase, cap) {\n  const phaseState = state.phases[phase];\n  if (!phaseState) return { allowed: true };\n  return {\n    allowed: phaseState.loop_count < cap,\n    current: phaseState.loop_count,\n    cap\n  };\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Part 8: Session Isolation Design\n\n**Problem:** Multiple agent sessions (e.g., Claude in one terminal, Codex in another) could clobber each other's state.\n\n**Solution inspired by Temporal's workflow task exclusivity:**\n\n1. On `wazir capture init`, generate a `session_id` (e.g., `ses-{uuid-v4-short}`). Store it in `pipeline-state.json`.\n2. On every CLI write operation, check that the caller's session ID matches. If mismatch, return an error: \"Session conflict: run owned by session `ses-abc`, current session is `ses-xyz`. Use `wazir capture takeover --run <id> --session <new-id>` to force.\"\n3. Hooks reading the state do NOT enforce session ID -- they just read. Session enforcement is a write-side concern.\n4. The `session_id` is passed to the CLI via `--session` flag or `WAZIR_SESSION_ID` environment variable. The session-start hook generates it and exports it.\n\n**Takeover protocol for recovery:**\n```\nwazir capture takeover --run <id> --session <new-session-id> --force\n```\nThis updates `session_id` and appends a `session_takeover` event to events.ndjson with the old and new session IDs. This is the crash-recovery mechanism -- if an agent dies, the next agent session takes over.\n\n---\n\n### Part 9: Crash Recovery Design\n\n**Inspired by Temporal's event replay, simplified for local execution:**\n\n1. **pipeline-state.json is always recoverable from events.ndjson.** The state file is a materialized view. If it's corrupted or missing, replay events:\n   ```\n   wazir capture rebuild --run <id>\n   ```\n   This reads events.ndjson line-by-line, applies each event to an empty state, and writes the result.\n\n2. **Consistency check on session start.** Compare `pipeline-state.json.integrity.event_count` against actual line count in `events.ndjson`. If they diverge, auto-rebuild.\n\n3. **Atomic writes prevent partial-write corruption.** The temp+rename protocol means the file is either the old version or the new version, never a half-written mix.\n\n4. **The `latest` pointer (already exists) enables finding the most recent run on restart.**\n\n5. **Incomplete phase detection.** If `current_phase_status` is `in_progress` but `timestamps.updated_at` is older than a configurable threshold (e.g., 30 minutes), the session-start hook can flag it as potentially stale and prompt for recovery.\n\n---\n\n### Part 10: Relationship to Existing Files\n\n**Migration path (no breaking changes):**\n\n| Current | Proposed | Migration |\n|---------|----------|-----------|\n| `status.json` | `pipeline-state.json` | `status.json` remains for backward compat; `pipeline-state.json` is the new authoritative source. Gradually migrate hooks to read from it. |\n| `events.ndjson` | `events.ndjson` (unchanged) | Append-only log remains as audit trail and recovery source |\n| `phase_prerequisites` in manifest | `phase_sequence` + `phases` in pipeline-state | The manifest declares the rules; pipeline-state records which ones have been satisfied |\n| `phase_loop_counts` in status.json | `phases[x].loop_count` in pipeline-state | Collocated with phase data instead of flat map |\n| `gating-rules.yaml` | `gating-rules.yaml` (unchanged) | Rules stay external; pipeline-state records gate verdicts |\n\n**Key improvement:** Today, checking \"can I enter the execute phase?\" requires:\n1. Read `status.json` (current phase)\n2. Scan `events.ndjson` for phase_exit events (O(n))\n3. Check filesystem for required artifacts\n4. Read manifest for prerequisites\n\nWith `pipeline-state.json`, it becomes:\n1. Read `pipeline-state.json`\n2. Check `phases.plan-review.gate.verdict === 'approved'` and `phases.plan-review.status === 'completed'`\n\nSingle file, single read, O(1).\n\n---\n\n### Summary of Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **pipeline-state.json is a materialized view of events.ndjson** -- not a replacement. Events remain the source of truth for audit; the state file is a read-optimized projection.\n2. **CLI writes, hooks read** -- strict separation prevents race conditions and keeps hooks fast.\n3. **Atomic writes via temp+rename** -- standard POSIX pattern, no locking needed for single-writer.\n4. **Session ID for isolation** -- lightweight alternative to Temporal's workflow task serialization.\n5. **Rebuild from events for recovery** -- simplified version of Temporal's deterministic replay.\n6. **Per-phase status + conclusion** -- adopted from GitHub Actions' job model, richer than boolean completed/not-completed.\n7. **Gate objects with rejection history** -- captures the full approval lifecycle, not just the final verdict.\n8. **Embedded phase_sequence** -- hooks don't need to parse pipeline.mdc or the manifest to know phase ordering.\n9. **Integrity checksum** -- enables detecting state/event divergence without replaying.\n10. **Backward compatible** -- status.json continues to work; pipeline-state.json is additive."}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2093,"cache_read_input_tokens":68845,"output_tokens":6223,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":2093},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZERgoxjq37kkpafzpNeZ","type":"assistant","uuid":"ca13c28f-8593-4e0d-a21f-fd473ff1c596","timestamp":"2026-03-20T13:42:08.150Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/mohamedabdallah/Work/Wazir","sessionId":"0c5a9bfa-6816-42b1-a97d-37ae7dad26c5","version":"2.1.80","gitBranch":"feat/remaining-6-fixes","slug":"mighty-wondering-giraffe"}
